scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;">\n<div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Head</div>\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Petteri_Taalas" title="Petteri Taalas">Petteri Taalas</a> (Secretary-General)<br/>\n<a href="/wiki/David_Grimes_(meteorologist)" title="David Grimes (meteorologist)">David Grimes</a> (President)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;">Website</th>\n<td><span class="url"><a class="external text" href="http://public.wmo.int" rel="nofollow">public<wbr/>.wmo<wbr/>.int</a></span></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The <b>World Meteorological Organization</b> (<b>WMO</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental organization</a> with a membership of 191 Member States and Territories. It originated from the <a href="/wiki/International_Meteorological_Organization" title="International Meteorological Organization">International Meteorological Organization</a> (IMO), which was founded in 1873. Established by the ratification of the <a class="external text" href="http://library.wmo.int/opac/doc_num.php?explnum_id=3137" rel="nofollow">WMO Convention</a> on 23 March 1950, WMO became the specialised agency of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> for <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">meteorology</a> (weather and <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a>), operational <a href="/wiki/Hydrology" title="Hydrology">hydrology</a> and related <a href="/wiki/Geophysics" title="Geophysics">geophysical sciences</a> a year later. Its current Secretary-General is <a href="/wiki/Petteri_Taalas" title="Petteri Taalas">Petteri Taalas</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> and the President of the World Meteorological Congress, its supreme body, is David Grimes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The Organization is <a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en/resources/wmo-building-conference-centre" rel="nofollow">headquartered</a> in Geneva, Switzerland.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Notes_and_references"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Notes and references</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_organization">The organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: The organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The World Meteorological Organization (WMO) is a specialized agency of the United Nations. It is the UN system\'s authoritative voice on the state and behavior of the Earth\'s atmosphere, its interaction with the oceans, the climate it produces and the resulting distribution of <a href="/wiki/Water_resources" title="Water resources">water resources</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_in_Brief_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMO_in_Brief-3">[3]</a></sup></p>\n<p>WMO has a membership of <a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en/about-us/members" rel="nofollow">191 Member States and Territories</a> as of February 2014. The <a class="external text" href="http://library.wmo.int/opac/doc_num.php?explnum_id=3137" rel="nofollow">Convention of the World Meteorological Organization</a> was signed 11 October 1947 and established upon ratification on 23 March 1950. WMO became the specialized agency of the United Nations in 1951 for meteorology (weather and climate), operational <a href="/wiki/Hydrology" title="Hydrology">hydrology</a> and related geophysical sciences. It originated from the <a href="/wiki/International_Meteorological_Organization" title="International Meteorological Organization">International Meteorological Organization</a> (IMO), which was founded in 1873.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_in_Brief_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-WMO_in_Brief-3">[3]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The WMO hierarchy:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>The <a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en/about-us/governance" rel="nofollow">World Meteorological Congress</a>, the supreme body of the Organization, determines policy. Each member state and territory is represented by a Permanent Representative with WMO when Congress meets every four years. Congress elects the President and Vice-Presidents of the Organization and members of the Executive Council; and appoints the Secretary-General.</li>\n<li>The Executive Council (EC) implements Congress decisions. It coordinates programmes, manages the budget, considers and acts on resolutions and recommendations from the regional associations and technical commissions, and studies and makes recommendations on matters affecting international meteorology and related activities. The Executive Council normally hold a session at least once a year.</li>\n<li>Six Regional Associations (RA) are responsible for the coordination of meteorological, hydrological and related activities within their respective Regions. They meet once every four years, and elect a president and vice-president. The president of each regional association is an ex officio member of the Executive Council.</li>\n<li><a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en/our-mandate/how-we-do-it/technical-commissions" rel="nofollow">Eight Technical Commissions</a> are responsible for studying meteorological and hydrological operational systems, applications and research. They establish methodology and procedures and make recommendations to Executive Council and the World Meteorological Congress.</li>\n<li><a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en/about-us/secretariat" rel="nofollow">The Secretariat</a> is headed by the Secretary-General, who is appointed by the World Meteorological Congress for a four-year term with a maximum tenure of 8 years. The Secretary-General appoints all staff, including the Deputy Secretary-General and the Assistant Secretary-General. The Secretariat currently has around 300 staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Functions">Functions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Functions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Weather, climate and the <a href="/wiki/Water_cycle" title="Water cycle">water cycle</a> shape almost every aspect of our lives. They can be benevolent and bring abundance and well-being, but they can also be dangerous and cause great damage: weather-, climate and water-related hazards account for nearly 90% of "natural" disasters. These powerful natural forces do not recognize national borders, thus global and regional cooperation is essential. Global data are needed to understand the behaviour of the Earth\xe2\x80\x99s atmosphere and its interaction with the land and oceans - whether it be to predict next week\xe2\x80\x99s weather or next year\xe2\x80\x99s climate, forecasters must have timely, quality-assured, standardized information coming from all corners of the world. Even the accuracy of a two-day weather forecast relies on observations from far beyond national borders. The World Meteorological Organization provides the framework for this essential international cooperation among the National Meteorological and Hydrological Services of its 191 Member States and Territories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmo_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-wmo-5">[5]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Weather">Weather</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Weather">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Thanks to the international coordination efforts of WMO, National Meteorological and Hydrological Services provide daily weather forecasts and early and reliable warnings of high-impact weather and climate events. These warnings help to save countless lives and to protect property and the environment from damage. They contribute to economic planning and decision-making, and help minimize the harm that weather, climate and water hazards can cause to socioeconomic development. The Organization also fosters collaboration between the National Meteorological and Hydrological Services to furthers the application of meteorology to public weather services, agriculture, aviation, shipping, energy, water resource management and many other economic sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmo_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-wmo-5">[5]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The first step in producing weather forecasts is to gather non-stop observations of the environment from around the world. Millions of observations are gathered worldwide every day by over 50 satellites, 400 moored buoys, 1 250 drifting buoys, 4 000 aircraft from around 40 commercial aircraft companies, 7 300 ships and 10 000 land-based observing stations. WMO develops the technical standards for designing these and other observing instruments and for ensuring that the collected data are quality controlled and comparable. Data that pass the test are fed into the complex numerical weather prediction models that National Meteorological Services use to produce weather forecasts, early warnings of storms and other natural hazards, air-quality forecasts, climate predictions and risk assessments. These forecasts and related products are broadcast in real time to the public and myriads of users worldwide. This enables governments to provide reliable and effective weather services to protect lives and property and ensure sustainable economic development and the general welfare of their citizens. To achieve these objectives, WMO advocates for broad, open data policies and maintains standardized data and exchange mechanisms. It also collaborates on the development of innovative data collection and delivery systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmo_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-wmo-5">[5]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The stations of the WMO Global Atmosphere Watch play a vital role in detecting climate variability and change by monitoring long-term changes in levels of greenhouse gases, solar radiation and other atmospheric components to assess their effects on people, climate, regional and urban air quality, and marine and terrestrial ecosystems. They project the magnitude and rate of climate change and related impacts such as sea-level rise. WMO publishes an annual <a class="external text" href="http://library.wmo.int/opac/index.php?lvl=notice_display&amp;id=3030#.WONyfnew1Bw" rel="nofollow">Greenhouse Gas Bulletin</a>, with details on atmospheric concentrations of long-lived greenhouse gases including carbon dioxide, methane and nitrous oxide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The WMO-led <a class="external text" href="http://www.gfcs-climate.org" rel="nofollow">Global Framework for Climate Services</a> (GFCS) guides the development of science-based climate information and services to support decision-making in climate-sensitive sectors. GFCS coordinates actions at the national, regional and global levels to enhance the quality, quantity and use of climate services. Climate information empowers countries to implement the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a> on climate change and promotes sustainable development. The GFCS enables public- and private-sector decision-makers to plan and adapt their activities and projects in anticipation of changing conditions. Seasonal climate forecasts, in particular, are increasingly used for agriculture and food security, disaster risk reduction, energy, public health, water resources and other sectors.</p>\n<p>The annually published <a class="external text" href="http://library.wmo.int/opac/index.php?lvl=notice_display&amp;id=97#.WOOzUnew1Bw" rel="nofollow">WMO Statements on the status of the World Climate</a> provides details of global, regional and national temperatures and extreme weather events. It also provides information on long-term climate change indicators include atmospheric concentrations of greenhouse gases, sea level rise, and sea ice extent. The year 2016 was the hottest year on record, with many weather and climate extremes, according to the most recent WMO report.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The World Meteorological Organization further supports climate change assessments by providing data and models and by hosting and co-sponsoring the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a> (IPCC), the <a href="/wiki/Global_Climate_Observing_System" title="Global Climate Observing System">Global Climate Observing System</a> (GCOS) and the <a href="/wiki/World_Climate_Research_Programme" title="World Climate Research Programme">World Climate Research Programme</a> (WCRP).</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Water is essential for the production of virtually all of our goods and services. It is the most important and widely used source of renewable energy - hydropower represents approximately 16% of total electricity production worldwide. The World Meteorological Organization promotes water-resource assessments by National Hydrological Services, which, in turn, provide the forecasts needed to plan water storage for domestic requirements, agricultural activities, hydroelectric power gener- ation and urban development.</p>\n<p>The Organization also assists National Hydrological Services to establish and maintain systems for acquiring and disseminating accurate and timely information on the water cycle for formulating integrated water-resource management strategies. Equipped with better hydrological information, assessments and forecasts, countries are able to independently assess their water resources and respond to threats of floods and drought.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="WMO_Strategic_Plan">WMO Strategic Plan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: WMO Strategic Plan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a class="external text" href="http://library.wmo.int/pmb_ged/wmo_1161_en.pdf" rel="nofollow">WMO Strategic Plan</a> sets the directions and priorities to guide the activities of Members and constituent bodies to enable the improvement of their core information, products and services, to maintain necessary infrastructures and to directly benefit from advancements in science and technology. This Plan emphasizes the following <b>key priorities</b>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>disaster risk reduction</li>\n<li>the Global Framework for Climate Services (GFCS)</li>\n<li>the WMO Integrated Global Observing System (WIGOS)</li>\n<li>aviation meteorological services</li>\n<li>polar and high mountain regions</li>\n<li>capacity development</li>\n<li>governance</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Contributions_to_Sustainable_Development_Goals">Contributions to Sustainable Development Goals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Contributions to Sustainable Development Goals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development</a> serves as the centerpiece for national and international policymaking over the next 15 years. It sets out 17 Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs) that the WMO community can contribute to at the national and international levels. National Meteorological and Hydrological Services (NMHSs) can benefit from the status of WMO as a Specialized Agency of the UN to engage with the 2030 Agenda. They can also draw on the partnerships that the WMO community continues to build with other communities, sectors and disciplines, for example, through national climate services and the <a class="external text" href="http://www.gfcs-climate.org/" rel="nofollow">Global Framework for Climate Services</a>. As policymakers and the general public gain a better understand of the <a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en/our-mandate/what-we-do/wmo-contributing-sustainable-development-goals-sdgs" rel="nofollow">WMO contribution to sustainable development</a>, National Meteorological and Hydrological Services can look forward to establishing an even stronger role in protecting life and property, and in building weather and climate resilience.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_codes">Meteorological codes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Meteorological codes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In keeping with its mandate to promote the standardization of meteorological observations, the WMO maintains numerous code forms for the representation and exchange of meteorological, oceanographical, and hydrological data. The traditional code forms, such as <a href="/wiki/SYNOP" title="SYNOP">SYNOP</a>, <a href="/wiki/CLIMAT" title="CLIMAT">CLIMAT</a> and <a href="/wiki/TEMP_(meteorology)" title="TEMP (meteorology)">TEMP</a>, are character-based and their coding is position-based. Newer WMO code forms are designed for portability, extensibility and universality. These are <a href="/wiki/BUFR" title="BUFR">BUFR</a>, CREX, and, for gridded geo-positioned data, <a href="/wiki/GRIB" title="GRIB">GRIB</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognitions_received">Recognitions received</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Recognitions received">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul>\n<li>The WMO and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> (UNEP) jointly created <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a> (IPCC) received the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> in 2007 "for their efforts to build up and disseminate greater knowledge about <a href="/wiki/Human_impact_on_the_environment" title="Human impact on the environment">anthropogenic</a> (man-made) climate change, and to lay the foundations for the measures that are needed to counteract such change."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Meteorological_Day">World Meteorological Day</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: World Meteorological Day">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WMO_%C5%BDeneva.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nWMO headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a> shared with the IPCC and the <a href="/wiki/Group_on_Earth_Observations" title="Group on Earth Observations">Group on Earth Observations</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li>World Meteorological Day is held annually on 23 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_public_outreach_materials">Main public outreach materials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Main public outreach materials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul>\n<li>The <a class="external text" href="https://www.wmocloudatlas.org/home.html" rel="nofollow">International Cloud Atlas</a> - On 23 March 2017, WMO released a completely revised and updated electronic version combining 19th century traditions with 21st century technology. The <a href="/wiki/International_Cloud_Atlas" title="International Cloud Atlas">International Cloud Atlas</a> was first published by WMO predecessor, IMO, in 1896. The new version contains hundreds of images submitted by meteorologists, photographers and cloud lovers from around the globe. It includes new classifications, including volutus, a roll cloud; clouds from human activities such as the contrail, a vapour trail sometimes produced by airplanes; and asperitas, a dramatic undulated cloud which captured the public imagination. It also features meteorological phenomena like rainbows, halos, snow devils and hailstones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="external text" href="http://library.wmo.int/opac/doc_num.php?explnum_id=3331" rel="nofollow">The World Meteorological Organization at a Glance</a></li>\n<li><a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en" rel="nofollow">WMO Public website</a></li>\n<li><a class="external text" href="http://youth.wmo.int" rel="nofollow">WMO for Youth</a></li>\n<li><a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en/resources/bulletin" rel="nofollow">WMO Bulletin</a> (twice annually)</li>\n<li><a class="external text" href="http://library.wmo.int/opac/index.php?lvl=notice_display&amp;id=3030#.WOO0n3ew1Bx" rel="nofollow">WMO Greenhouse Gas Bulletin</a> (annually)</li>\n<li><a class="external text" href="http://library.wmo.int/opac/index.php?lvl=notice_display&amp;id=97#.WOOzUnew1Bw" rel="nofollow">WMO Statements on the Status of the World Climate</a> (annually)</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="WMO_awards_and_prizes">WMO awards and prizes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en/about-us/awards/professor-mariolopoulos-award" rel="nofollow">Professor Mariolopoulus Award</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Milestones">Milestones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Milestones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><b>1853</b> First International Meteorological Conference (Brussels)</p>\n<p><b>1873</b> International Meteorological Organization established (predecessor of WMO)</p>\n<p><b>1947</b> WMO Convention agreed unanimously by Conference of Directors (Washington, DC)</p>\n<p><b>1950</b> WMO Convention enters into force on 23 March</p>\n<p><b>1951</b> WMO becomes a specialized agency of the United Nations</p>\n<p><b>1957</b> Global Ozone Observing System set up</p>\n<p><b>1957/1958</b> <a href="/wiki/International_Geophysical_Year" title="International Geophysical Year">International Geophysical Year</a></p>\n<p><b>1963</b> World Weather Watch (WWW) launched</p>\n<p><b>1971</b> Tropical Cyclone project established (upgraded to Tropical Cyclone Programme in 1980)</p>\n<p><b>1972</b> Operational Hydrology Programme established</p>\n<p><b>1976</b> WMO issues first international assessment of the state of global ozone</p>\n<p><b>1977</b> Integrated Global Ocean Services System (IGOSS) established jointly by WMO and <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Oceanographic_Commission" title="Intergovernmental Oceanographic Commission">Intergovernmental Oceanographic Commission</a> (IOC)</p>\n<p><b>1978/1979</b> Global Weather Experiment and Monsoon Experiments under the Global Atmospheric Research Programme</p>\n<p><b>1979</b> First <a href="/wiki/World_Climate_Conference" title="World Climate Conference">World Climate Conference</a> (leads to the establishment of the WMO World Climate Programme)</p>\n<p><b>1985</b> <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Convention_for_the_Protection_of_the_Ozone_Layer" title="Vienna Convention for the Protection of the Ozone Layer">Vienna Convention for the Protection of the Ozone Layer</a></p>\n<p><b>1987</b> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montreal_Protocol_on_Substances_that_Deplete_the_Ozone_Layer" title="Montreal Protocol on Substances that Deplete the Ozone Layer">Montreal Protocol on Substances that Deplete the Ozone Layer</a></p>\n<p><b>1988</b> <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a> (IPCC) established, co-sponsored by WMO and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> (UNEP)</p>\n<p><b>1989</b> <a href="/wiki/Global_Atmosphere_Watch" title="Global Atmosphere Watch">Global Atmosphere Watch</a> established</p>\n<p><b>1990</b> Second <a href="/wiki/World_Climate_Conference" title="World Climate Conference">World Climate Conference</a>; <a href="/wiki/International_Decade_for_Natural_Disaster_Reduction" title="International Decade for Natural Disaster Reduction">International Decade for Natural Disaster Reduction</a></p>\n<p><b>1991</b> WMO/UNEP convene first meeting of the Intergovernmental Negotiating Committee of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change" title="United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change">United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change</a></p>\n<p><b>1992</b> The <a href="/wiki/Global_Climate_Observing_System" title="Global Climate Observing System">Global Climate Observing System</a> established</p>\n<p><b>1993</b> <a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en/programmes/hydrology-and-water-resources-programme" rel="nofollow">World Hydrological Cycle Observing System</a> (WHYCOS) launched</p>\n<p><b>1995</b> <a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en/resources/bulletin/climate-services-\xe2\x80\x93-transitioning-from-clips-gfcs-0" rel="nofollow">Climate Information and Prediction Services</a> (CLIPS) established</p>\n<p><b>1998</b> Scientific Assessment of Ozone Depletion</p>\n<p><b>1999</b> Inauguration of new <a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en/resources/wmo-building-conference-centre" rel="nofollow">WMO headquarters</a> in Geneva</p>\n<p><b>2005</b> <a href="/wiki/Group_on_Earth_Observations" title="Group on Earth Observations">Group on Earth Observations</a> (GEO) Secretariat established</p>\n<p><b>2007/2008</b> <a href="/wiki/International_Polar_Year" title="International Polar Year">International Polar Year</a></p>\n<p><b>2009</b> Third <a href="/wiki/World_Climate_Conference" title="World Climate Conference">World Climate Conference</a> establishes <a class="external text" href="http://www.gfcs-climate.org" rel="nofollow">Global Framework for Climate Services</a></p>\n<p><b>2014</b> <a class="external text" href="https://public.wmo.int/en/resources/gender-equality" rel="nofollow">Conference on the Gender Dimensions of Weather and Climate Services</a></p>\n<p><b>2015</b> <a href="/wiki/Sendai_Framework_for_Disaster_Risk_Reduction" title="Sendai Framework for Disaster Risk Reduction">Sendai Framework for Disaster Risk Reduction 2015\xe2\x80\x932030</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development</a>; <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a> reached at the Conference of the Parties (COP21) of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNFCCC" title="UNFCCC">UNFCCC</a></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership">Membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>As of February 2014, WMO Members include a total of 185 Member States and 6 Member Territories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Members_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Members-16">[16]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Ten United Nations member states are not members of WMO: <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a> are WMO Members but non-members of the United Nations. <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">states with limited recognition</a> are not members of either organization.</p>\n<p>The six WMO Member Territories are the <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British</a> Caribbean Territories (joint meteorological organisation and membership),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Members_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Members-16">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a>, Hong Kong, <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Cura\xc3\xa7ao">Cura\xc3\xa7ao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a> (joint meteorological service and membership)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Members_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-Members-16">[16]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a>. id="Region_IV_.28North_America.2C_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean.29">Region IV (North America, Central America and the Caribbean)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Region IV (North America, Central America and the Caribbean)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Region IV consists of the states of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, including three European states with dependencies within the region. It has a total of 25 member states and 2 member territories. region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Meteorological_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: States with membership in more than one region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>A total of ten member states have membership in more than one region. Two nations are members to four different regions, while eight are members of two regions.
